Free Talk

On Advocating Literature 200

— Hu Lu

Not long ago, a gentleman saw the phrases "If literature doesn't die, disaster won't cease" and immediately protested loudly. He also complained that the government had not invested in literature; he said that the country sends students abroad to study science, but science hasn't flourished, yet the country hasn't advocated for literature.

This statement, in reality, isn't entirely true. From ancient times to the present, hasn't the "ruler" always promoted literature? To put it further back, in ancient times, any enlightened ruler who "valued literature" would give literary people high positions: This is a "common historical occurrence"; even if some literary people couldn't comprehend the "emperor's heart," as long as they could provide entertainment for the emperor, they would inevitably be rewarded with a small official position: This can also be verified by history. Only a foolish ruler like Emperor Yang of Sui would kill literary people because he couldn't create good lines like "Swallows fallen from the empty beam," but Emperor Yang ultimately lost his country. He didn't understand the rules of being an emperor; being an emperor means "promoting" literature, not competing with literary people in intelligence.

Historical records testify to this. Looking at contemporary measures, take the massive recent budget as an example. The amount of money spent on promoting literature is indeed too small. But, unbeknownst to some, in today's impoverished rural areas, being able to spend a little money on literature already shows enthusiasm for promotion. Or do some think that loyal literary people should have official positions, but because they don't, that is seen as not promoting literature? Unbeknownst to some, this way of thinking is also a bit of an "anachronism." In ancient times with emperors, the method of promoting literature was to bestow official positions. Now, we are a modern country without an emperor, so how can we still use that old tune!

To sum it up in one sentence: In modern Chinese history, except for the reigns of Kangxi and Qianlong, no era has paid more attention to promoting literature than the present! However, Kangxi and Qianlong frequently displayed banners of "Imperial Approval" and "Imperial Decree" to highlight the characteristics of the imperial system. Now, in the Republic of China, there are naturally other methods of promotion.

Loneliness 201

— Fei Er

Loneliness is like a bottomless abyss, filled with darkness. Loneliness is also like the shadow of the night, its form elusive.

One who deeply tastes loneliness is a lonely heart, a lonely heart like a seasoned and worldly-wise traveler. The more one returns from a lively place, the more one can taste the flavor of loneliness. The more bustling the past was, the more the ensuing loneliness feels lonely. If the bustle were to disappear, loneliness would fundamentally cease to exist in this world.

After the Parisian citizens' fervent revolution, the guillotine and the gallows followed. Consequently, a great shadow of loneliness deeply shrouded the hearts of all citizens. Following the bloody revolution in Soviet Russia, the ensuing economic recovery led to the suicide of the poet Mayakovsky, who couldn't adapt to the second wave of excitement. He was killed by a lonely heart.

We naturally also have our post-excitement loneliness, but this kind of loneliness is left for those who cannot speculate or adapt to savor.

Our era is an era of manufacturing loneliness. Turbulent times have disturbed the minds of the clever; layer upon layer of oppression has also disturbed the nerves of the weak. Thus, loneliness is a gift to both the clever and the weak.

The ignorant and the strong do not experience loneliness. If they do, it is a different kind of loneliness.

Clever people also have times when they are not lonely, such as when they sell their souls, or deceive or numb themselves in various ways. However, when the soul or drunken dream awakens, the loneliness at that time will be an extraordinary loneliness, accompanied by an unusually painful loneliness.

The result of loneliness is either suicide or madness, or at the very least it will cloud the mind, causing restlessness, making one feel there is nowhere to place even one's own body.

It is said that artists, literary people, and sensitive youths are most susceptible to "loneliness sickness," and there have been many examples of this throughout history. Because their hearts are not understood by people, their works are not appreciated by people, or a great era of sudden change makes them feel lost, they feel alone, bored, and feel the need to go mad or die. They are indeed killed by cleverness, but they are killed by loneliness.

When loneliness strikes, reason sometimes loses its effectiveness. A person without loneliness will never have loneliness. And for a person with loneliness, even if you put him in a crowded dance hall, dancing wildly, he will still feel lonely, or even a more intense loneliness.

However, the morbid state of loneliness is not entirely unavoidable. When a person is working intently and passionately, the shadow of loneliness avoids him; when the era is progressing towards upward brightness, the era will not have era-specific loneliness.

As for the motivation for writing this article, the purpose is clearly to kill a bit of loneliness in time.

"Let us not have loneliness!" was shouted loudly in a moment of deep loneliness.

Notes on Lili Kober (Part 1 Continued) 202

— Xu Maoyong

Two

However, Shanghai is Shanghai, and China is China. Knowing Shanghai doesn't mean you know China. Before her trip to Beijing, Lili Kober ultimately knew nothing about China. Not only were her observations limited, but she hadn't even heard much from others.

This isn't entirely due to language barriers. She was born in Austria, studied at the University of Frankfurt in Germany, and German is her native language. In recent years, she worked at the Putilov Works factory in Soviet Russia, and she can also speak Russian, in addition to French and English. Shanghai has plenty of people who speak "English," so why couldn't she converse with many people? However, the question is what should people tell her? For example, the Mr. Willys she met, those kind and frequently cheerful, plump Western gentlemen, only told her things like:

"Chinese people's lives are very good. They have no needs and no worries. They have enough to eat and are often very happy. Yes, these ragged people, at first glance, seem very unpleasant. But after getting used to each other, you don't feel anything. If you live here long enough, you'll get used to them too."

How to get used to them? For example, when Mr. Willy takes a rickshaw on Nanjing Road and a piece of sweet potato peel suddenly flies over and dirties his clothes, he can jump out of the rickshaw and randomly grab a Chinese person to beat, or call the tall Indian policemen wearing turbans to arrest people. Or, when walking on the road and running into a Chinese person, the Chinese person should give way, not Mr. Willy...

But these words made Lili Kober "angry." She didn't want to listen to them. What she wanted to hear were the words of Chinese people. However, the question came up again: what should the Chinese people tell her?

For example, even the situation in the Chinese literary scene that I'm very familiar with, when she asked me, I couldn't simply summarize it. My answer, written in words, took two nights of thinking.

We ourselves don't really know what method we can use to tell others about everything. Therefore, whenever foreign guests come to China, even if they are investigators, we often treat them as "encyclopedias" and interrogate them, leaving them no time to interrogate us.

Three

George Bernard Shaw shook the world, creating excitement everywhere, that was natural. Even if black Hughes or French Zhang Henshui or Georges Ebella came to China, they wouldn't be neglected. But someone as desolate as Kober was truly unprecedented. When she first arrived in Shanghai, she had to find the Soviet consulate, and the consulate introduced her to a news agency, and Mr. C from the news agency introduced her to a few literary youths. Only then did she find an American school and stay there. Mr. C once treated her to a delicious meal at the New Asia Restaurant. After that, there was only one public banquet by three literary groups. The number of guests attending this public banquet was only five, which was very dishonorable. Although this also fortunately avoided many smoky attacks, the scheduled dishes were not finished after all, which she and everyone else felt was a pity.

Before taking their seats, when talking about The True Story of Ah Q, she asked caringly about the recent situation of the author of this novel. I said with a smile:

"He's coming soon."

Because I knew that the person in charge that day had invited Mr. Lu Xun, she was so happy that she was almost excited. However, in the end, Mr. Lu Xun didn't come, saying that he had suffered from heatstroke and couldn't come out. Although Kober didn't express it at the time, two days later, when Mr. Ren went to visit her, she asked with regret:

"Was Mr. Lu Xun's absence because he looked down on me?"

After listening to Mr. Ren's explanation of the real reason, she was happy again.

Casual Literary Talks 203

— Hua Yu

(8) How to Hand Over?

The fact of handing over writing to the masses already existed since the late Qing Dynasty.

"[Don't beat the drum, don't beat the gong, listen to me sing a song of peace...]" was a sanctioned folk song for educational affairs; in addition, scholar-officials also ran some vernacular newspapers, but the idea was only that everyone should understand it, not necessarily be able to write it. "The Thousand Character Primer for Common People" carried a hint of the possibility of being able to write, but it was only enough for keeping accounts and writing letters. If you wanted to write out what you were thinking in your heart, its limited number of characters was not enough. For example, prison indeed gives people a piece of land, but it has restrictions, only allowing you to stand, sit, lie down, and rest within this circle, and you absolutely cannot run out of the established iron fence.

Lao Nai'an and Zhao Yuanren both had simplified characters, which were very advanced and could write words according to their sounds. At the beginning of the Republic of China, the Ministry of Education wanted to create an alphabet. They were both members. Mr. Lao sent a representative, and Mr. Wang came in person. For the issue of the preservation or abolition of entering tones, he had a great battle with Mr. Wu Zhihui, a battle that made Mr. Wu's stomach cave in and his cotton pants fall down. But in the end, after several deliberations, they created something called the "National Phonetic Alphabet." At that time, many people thought it could replace Chinese characters, but in reality it still didn't work, because it was ultimately just a simplified version of square characters, just like Japanese "kana." It's okay to insert a few or annotate them next to Chinese characters, but if you want it to be the main force, it will be mixed up when writing and will strain your eyes when reading. The members at that time called it the "National Phonetic Alphabet" because they deeply knew its range of ability. Looking at Japan again, they have those who advocate reducing Chinese characters and those who advocate pulling together the alphabet, but no one advocates using only "kana."

A better approach is using Romanization. Zhao Yuanren is the most sophisticated scholar of Romanization, but I don't quite understand it. Using the world-renowned Roman alphabet [now even Turkey has adopted it], each word is a string, very clear, which is good. But to a layman like me, it seems that the spelling is still too cumbersome. To be precise, it inevitably has to be cumbersome, but being so cumbersome makes it "difficult" again, which hinders popularization. It would be best to have another kind of simple but not crude thing.

We can study this kind of new "Romanization" method. There is a small book called "Latinization of Chinese Writing" in "Daily International Literature Selections," and a copy of "Language Science" recorded in the combined issue of the 6th and 7th issues of "World" in the second year, which both introduce this thing. The price is cheap. Those who are interested should buy it and read it. It only has twenty-eight letters, and the spelling is easy to learn. "Person" is Rhen, "house" is Fangz, "I eat fruit" is Wu Chgoz, "He is a worker" is Ta shgungrhen. It is now being tested among overseas Chinese and has seen results. It's just Northern Mandarin. But I think that after all, more people in China speak Northern Mandarin [not Beijing Mandarin]. In the future, if there really is a common language that is used everywhere, the main force will probably still be Northern Mandarin. For now, just make some reasonable additions and subtractions to make it consistent with the sounds unique to each locality, and it can be used in any remote rural area.

Then, as long as you recognize the twenty-eight letters, learn a little spelling and writing, anyone can write and understand it, except for lazy people and those with low abilities. Moreover, it also has a good advantage, which is that it writes quickly. Americans say that time is money; but I think: time is life. Pointlessly wasting other people's time is actually no different from plotting to take money and lives. However, people like us sitting and enjoying the cool breeze, chatting idly, are an exception.

10 + 10 = 20 Years Old 204

— TK

Little Sanzi 205

— Zhou Lengjia

Little Sanzi, be good, don't cry, Daddy will sing a mountain song for you to listen to: your mother has gone to the city to be a wet nurse, even if you cry yourself hoarse she won't hear your voice.

It is your destiny to have no milk to eat, who told you to be born poor! The children of the rich open their mouths to eat another woman's milk, the children of the poor can't even get close to their own mother!

There's famine everywhere this year, many adults are starving just like you. If you don't have milk, you can drink some plain water, some plain water can also save your hungry stomach.

The weather is not dry this year, it looks like a disaster is inevitable in the second half of the year! Little Sanzi, be good, don't cry, Daddy will do a cat washing its face for you to see.

Younger Brother (7) 206

— Zhou Wen

"Younger brother, don't gamble with those soldiers, brother!" I said.

"Um, um,..." one sentence.

"Younger brother, if you have nothing to do, brother will teach you some books," I said again.

"Um, um,..." two sentences.

I said again.

"Younger brother..."

"Um,..." he widened his big eyes, took the lighter I gave him that I had just bought from the provincial capital, and left again.

Later, I often heard about him gambling with the soldiers, even quarreling. Everyone was very worried. Coincidentally, at this time, the troops on our side started a war with the troops stationed in our hometown, and they had already won on the front line. That relative said happily:

"Good, when they attack your hometown, your mother will lock him up!"

When going on patrol on the road, I really wanted to call him to go with us to the rear, but I couldn't find him anywhere; I was especially worried on the day of the attack on my hometown, Lion Tiger Ridge. The opposing troops were holding the ridge tightly, scattering a line of skirmishers several miles long along the ridge, looking down at a small market town that we were approaching. Standing at the head of the town, the bridgehead on the ridge could be seen clearly in the middle of the charge, bullets whizzing past our heads like bees. It is said that our advance troops have already charged up, and that relative has also charged up, from the front. Oh, my younger brother is only fourteen years old, how can those small hands operate that small gun!

When we defeated the enemy and entered the city, stepping on many dead and half-dead bodies, my eyes searched urgently among them. On the road, I grabbed this person and asked, grabbed that person and asked. When I got home, my mother said that my younger brother rode a wild horse into the city with the troops, and he looked pitifully small on the horse, but as soon as he came back and ate half a bowl of rice, he jumped back on the horse and ran off as if he was afraid of being caught by someone. Although, my mother's words carried a bit of pride. Because there were neighbors around, she spoke even louder.

Page 18

Economic Supplement

How to Rescue the Current Disaster Victims 207

— Duan Sheng

Floods and droughts are unpredictable, and disasters have occurred in every era. Therefore, a good government must make these unpredictable floods and droughts, and the disasters that occur in every era, gradually disappear without a trace, preventing them before they happen. If rescue only begins after a disaster has already occurred, the people have already suffered.

The ancient ways of disaster relief mostly drew from the "Famine Administration" section of the Zhou Rituals, with additions and subtractions. The Famine Administration has eleven aspects: first, distributing benefits; second, reducing taxes; third, delaying punishments; fourth, easing labor demands; fifth, relaxing trade restrictions; sixth, eliminating unnecessary controls; seventh, reducing ceremonial observances; eighth, suppressing mourning; ninth, increasing music; tenth, encouraging marriage; eleventh, seeking divine guidance; twelfth, eliminating bandits. As for how those in positions of authority should handle a world of disaster and famine:

The Record of Rituals, Jade Ornaments says:

[If the year is unfavorable, the ruler wears coarse cloth and a hairpin of plain wood, levies no tolls on bridges and passes, does not tax mountains and marshes, suspends public works, and high officials are not allowed to build carriages.]

Mozi says:

[In lean years, officials from scholars and officials down lose one-fifth of their salaries; in droughts, they lose two-fifths; in calamitous times, they lose three-fifths; in times of scarcity, they lose four-fifths; in great famines, they receive no salary at all, only food.]

Guliang Zhuan says:

[In the rituals of great famine, the ruler does not eat elaborate meals, platforms and pavilions are not plastered, the roads to the watchtowers are neglected and not cleared, officials wear plain clothes, sacrifices to spirits are reduced. These are the rituals of great famine.]

It is clear that ancient disaster relief had established rules. Compared to those who see a disaster and do not help, or use disaster relief solely for their own benefit, how should one proceed? Those in positions of authority should reduce salaries, decrease their meals, and forgo entertainment in disaster years, to show that they share the people's suffering. This is better than later generations, who only hear the sound of disaster relief but see no one doing it, and still indulge in extravagance, debauchery, drunken singing, and senseless behavior as before. The "Cloud Han" poem in the Book of Songs is a work of King Yi of Zhou lamenting drought and disaster; later generations still read it with deep longing, and the people of that time could not but sympathize. This is why he was able to achieve a middling reign. The poem says:

[The drought is excessive, the mountains and rivers are parched. The drought demon rages, like fire and burning. My heart dreads the heat, my anxiety is like smoke. The assembled officials do not heed me. Oh, Heavenly God, would that you would let me escape!]

Even in later dynasties, even the most immoral rulers would issue edicts blaming themselves when faced with great droughts and disasters. Although they were acting insincerely, they at least showed some concern for the disaster victims.

The present age is not the ancient age, and the intentions of the people of today are not the same as those of the ancients. Moreover, the disasters of today are no less severe than those of ancient times. Those who suffer the most are usually the areas known for their wealth and prosperity. However, they are either suffering from the aftermath of war or the aftermath of great disasters, struggling to recover. The bankruptcy of rural areas and the emptiness of granaries are a common phenomenon. The arrival of drought is like adding frost to snow, suffering displacement only to face wandering. People are reduced to lifelessness, plagued by hunger and cold, and either contemplate murder or resort to desperate measures. All of this is a loss to the state and society, and a breeding ground for chaos.

In the autumn of the twentieth year of the Republic (1931), great floods affected the provinces of Jiangsu, Anhui, Hubei, and Henan. At that time, the emotions of those who heard of the disaster and rose to provide relief were passionate and intense. The scope of this year's drought is greater than the great flood of 1931. The damage suffered by the disaster victims, while not as complete as the washing away of fields, houses, livestock, and tools by the great flood, is no less severe than the aftermath of the great flood, considering the thousands of miles of barren land, the lack of harvest, and the interruption of life. Western Zhejiang is known for its wealth, but in recent years, farmers have mostly used miscellaneous grains for food and filled their bellies with sweet potatoes and taro. The reason is that agricultural products are worthless and silk cocoons are not moving, leaving them with almost no income. Moreover, exorbitant taxes and levies are the ultimate burden on farmers. All daily necessities, from needles to thread, depend on the cities, which in turn rely on foreign countries. Money only flows out of the rural areas and does not come in. It would be against all reason if they did not go bankrupt. Now, they are hit by a severe drought. Initially, rice seedlings were planted everywhere, and everyone hoped they would survive, so they spared no effort in watering them day and night, hoping that heaven would send rain and a harvest. However, heaven ultimately did not send rain, and the rivers and ponds dried up. Not only was there no water to irrigate the rice, but there was also a serious problem with drinking water. At this point, the efforts and debts of the farmers were all absorbed by the scorching sun, leaving them with nothing. Countless people are lying in bed, starving and waiting for help. Countless people are seeking a livelihood in the cities (which are already suffering from unemployment and cannot accommodate everyone). Countless more are preparing to flee to the four directions. However, society is indifferent to this, and the authorities are oblivious. The arrival of a flood is vast and overwhelming, engulfing mountains and hills, like an acute illness that is frightening and indescribable, deeply stimulating and easily arousing sympathy. A drought is like a slow-acting disease, lingering and unnoticed. People underestimate it, but as its symptoms deepen day by day, it becomes impossible to remedy. However, the biggest reason for society's indifference is the depression of all industries and the helplessness of all undertakings, which is not just the case with droughts. In addition, the success of previous disaster relief efforts must be attributed to the mobilization of various charities in Shanghai. However, in recent years, there have been too many relief efforts, with huge expenditures. Revenues have also been affected by the depression of all industries, making it impossible to raise funds. Most well-known charities are in debt. Therefore, apart from setting up altars to pray for rain, there is little active relief work. Compared to the great flood of 1931, when various charities distributed relief and the municipal government set up shelters, the enthusiasm is much less now! This is also a sign of the downturn in relief efforts. Therefore, the drought is becoming more and more serious, while Shanghai is in a state of peace and happiness. Apart from the high price of grain, it is hard to see any signs of disaster. It is thought that major cities are the same. Therefore, there is an indication that there is no need to restrict the price of rice, because they only see the superficial prosperity of the cities and have not seen the tragic and profound reality of the rural areas. Therefore, in the present age, being able to provide relief after a disaster has already occurred is still considered good governance. Preventing disasters before they happen is far beyond reach.

Relieving disasters is like putting out a fire, which speaks to the urgency of the situation. If it is delayed, the people will be displaced and become starving corpses on the side of the road. The disaster today is also urgent. Paper publicity never fails to proclaim prosperity; relief plans never fail to be grand. But if we wait for the success of the plan before starting relief, will we not be seeking our people in a dried fish shop? The ancients believed that official relief was inferior to voluntary relief, because official relief involved complicated procedures, such as investigating the disaster from the county, then the prefecture, then the circuit, then the governor, then reaching the department, then submitting a memorial, then receiving a reply, and then distributing relief. The process was cumbersome, slow, and criticized by the world. However, there are also ways to remedy the situation, such as local officials assessing the disaster and issuing timely relief from the granaries, which is called urgent relief. Therefore, if local officials truly value the livelihood of the people, they should consider how to handle the situation when the disaster is developing or has already occurred, starting from the moment the disaster signs appear. If they cannot plan in advance and do not think of exerting effort when the disaster strikes, even if the disaster is not deep, such delays will inevitably deepen it.

The government's disaster relief is a kind of repayment for the people's contributions. Since the people usually contribute their wealth to the government, when there is a real disaster and they have no food, the government should use public funds to help the people. In the past, in years of disaster, the government would exempt taxes, issue grain from the granaries, divert the grain tribute, and use regular funds. If that was not enough, it would allocate funds from the imperial treasury or seek assistance from neighboring provinces. However, due to the corruption of the bureaucracy, disaster relief became a shortcut for officials to get rich, and the benefits did not reach the people. However, this is different from those who lack conscience and ignore the disaster.

Disaster relief must start with investigating the disaster. If the investigation is thorough and detailed, the disaster relief will be effective. If the disaster situation is unclear, there is no way to provide relief; if the disaster victims are unclear, there is no way to implement relief. Therefore, whether it is work relief, loan relief, distribution relief, cooking relief, or sheltering and comforting, unless the local disaster depth, strength, number of elderly, weak, strong, young, classification of the poor, village to town distances, general situation of the society, is clearly understood, it is difficult to obtain an effective plan. Disaster investigation is the basis for disaster relief. If the disaster investigation personnel do not conduct on-site inspections, even if they do, and their experience is insufficient, once they enter the countryside, the environment suddenly changes, and they are at a loss as to what is important and what is not. And the disaster victims know that the purpose of the disaster investigation is to provide relief, they often fabricate disaster situations, over-report the number of people, and prepare for a place to request relief. The difficulties in this are described in detail by the ancients, and it is not difficult to consult relevant books on famine administration.

Regarding disaster situation investigations, it seems that it should be more convenient than before. Towns and villages already have full-time personnel such as district chiefs, as well as local police and baojia, etc. If they do it practically, it will not be difficult to complete. However, the easiest places to create problems in investigation:

(1) Investigators do not conduct practical inspections, and create behind closed doors; for example, some say that when checking the household registration, they multiply the number of households by [eight], and when asked why, they say [a family of eight can be without hunger], every family has eight members, so multiply by eight. This kind of scheme to fabricate household registration books is especially common when handling elections. If disaster investigation is also done like this, it is no different from not investigating, and will only lead to failure.

(2) Local government officials, in order to shirk responsibility in the future, always like to report the disaster situation as too serious. If the disaster situation investigation in the future is not as severe as reported, they will cover it up by reducing the report. If they do not investigate, they can get more relief funds. Recently, many counties have reported disasters with exaggerated words, and many have been revealed by higher authorities, which shows that the county officials' reports of famine cannot be fully believed. Some county officials report disasters, but still do not know what the disaster is.

(3) After the disaster investigation, it is necessary to add a re-investigation. This is for serious disaster relief, so that those with minor disasters do not get more relief benefits, and those with serious disasters do not cry silently. It should be done quickly, and actions should not be slow, and procedures should not be cumbersome. It is important to know that the disaster victims are eagerly awaiting relief, and providing relief one day earlier will reduce their suffering by one day.

Before the investigation and survey, for serious disaster relief that cannot be delayed, start with emergency relief first, and then conduct regular relief. The length of the relief period depends on the severity of the disaster, the local situation, and the time when the new grain enters the market. As for the method of relief, it is no more than the following:

Relief (A) Work relief | Relief through work (B) (1) Food (2) Silver (3) Clothing (4) Medicine (C) Cooking relief porridge (D) Price control | Rice (E) Loan relief Food seeds farm capital (F) Sheltering | Supply food and lodging

Work relief is to provide wages for labor. In drought years, work relief is used to dredge rivers and dig ponds, which is the best policy for preventing future floods and droughts. However, this is limited to the strong, and the elderly and weak cannot receive relief, and those who are unable to do labor cannot receive relief. Providing relief by distributing food and money on the spot should vary according to the situation. If food is very scarce and it is very difficult to obtain food, then food should be provided as relief. If local transportation is convenient, but there is poverty after the disaster and people cannot afford to buy food, then money should be provided as relief. Cooking relief has both advantages and disadvantages, and the ancients discussed it in detail. I believe that for temporary emergencies, porridge relief may be possible. If the relief period is longer, porridge factories cannot be set up everywhere, and those who seek food still have the hardship of traveling and being rejected. From a human perspective, it is better to give them money and let them dispose of it freely. Price control can only be implemented when the price of rice is high and it is difficult to buy food, but not to the point where people cannot afford to buy it. If the disaster is already deep and the people are all poor, how can they afford to buy food with price control? Therefore, when the disaster is already deep, there is only one way to provide relief. Loan relief and distribution relief, one is gratuitous; the other is for repayment | repayment in the future. Before the investigation proves that there is no disaster, and the people have difficulty in food, the standard is to get relief rice. I believe that in the current situation of serious disaster and difficult fundraising, it is possible to consider the situation of the disaster victims and implement loans in parallel. Seeds are very important for the harvest in the coming year, but in disaster years, they are often used to fill hunger for emergency relief. It is best for the government to issue them free of charge, and only resort to loans as a last resort. After the disaster, the people lack agricultural capital, so we should prepare to establish agricultural loans in local areas or credit cooperatives, so that the disaster farmers can receive assistance, so as not to hinder the progress of their cultivation. In the future, there will be a harvest, and there will be granaries to maintain it, so that there is no need to worry about low grain prices harming farmers. As for sheltering, it should be limited to the elderly, weak, women and children who are difficult to survive. Sheltering is not easy to handle. When crowds gather in one place, it is easy to cause trouble, and it is also easy to cause epidemics, which is costly and difficult. Therefore, if there are places to stay and not be displaced, it is possible to provide more relief without sheltering. If there is a danger of women and children being sold, and the elderly and weak have the pain of being displaced, it is necessary to provide sheltering.

The ways to relieve disasters are not the same, and the way to implement them should also be considered by the relief workers according to the situation of each area. However, because people's hearts are difficult to predict, and the people's situation is complicated, there is no good policy for relief, which is a common lament of ancient and modern times. Therefore, whether the relief is really beneficial to the disaster victims depends on whether the relief workers are sincerely coming to relieve the disaster. Those who have sympathy for the disaster victims will definitely think of reducing the suffering of the disaster victims, and the disaster victims will receive more benefits, and vice versa. However, given the extent of the disaster area, how can we get all the right people? The good and the bad are mixed together, which is also the same in ancient and modern times. Especially those who are self-interested and accustomed to encroaching. The feeling of having governance but no one to govern, and the changed appearance of a butcher who eats disasters regardless of the suffering of the disaster victims, can we guarantee that there will be none today, I am afraid there will be more. So when providing relief, how can we not hope that those responsible will be cautious in selecting people! Do not think that it is a good idea to place relatives and friends, and do not call for voluntary service. Voluntary service cannot last long. Not all relief workers are like the presiding officers who do not worry about their livelihoods and take benevolence as their mission. They mostly come to solve temporary livelihood problems. Even if it is not for livelihood, their travel expenses, food expenses, and accommodation also cost money, so it is necessary to give some public funds. Therefore, voluntary service can only save those who take benevolence as their mission, and cannot be required of all full-time relief workers. Relief workers often use relief funds for disaster relief, and should make every penny reach the disaster victims, so the intention of saving the living expenses of relief workers is good. But do not think that relief workers have difficulty in living, or encroach secretly, or even waste publicly, then the damage to the relief funds is even greater. If it is known that they are maintaining their lives and encroaching on the funds, and they are not investigated, then it is tacitly allowed that there is no wrongdoing, which is even more unreasonable. Zhen the treasure relief funds, is the responsibility of the relief workers, and those who donate money and food are for disaster relief, not for relief workers, so no relief funds should be used for relief workers. But rather than the name of voluntary service that is actually dirty, why not pay a reasonable salary, strictly control their income and expenditure examination for more healing. The most suitable method is that the relief public funds are paid from local public funds, except for the various sales groups or individuals who voluntarily undertake them, and the relief personnel are transferred from local public officials (belonging to party and government local autonomy organs and various public groups). These all have their deserved salaries, and serving the local area to provide disaster relief is also their duty, (if they always want to show that they are public officials, using them to provide disaster relief, there are more failures than successes, this should also be considered.) As for the expenses of the relief headquarters and the funds used for starting relief, they should be paid from the provincial treasury or the national treasury, so that the relief funds donated by all parties can be used on the disaster victims.

Relief is difficult, fundraising is also difficult, the public hope that those with money will give money, and those with strength will give strength, to benefit the disaster victims, it is necessary that the disaster situation has aroused the sympathy of the general public, and the relief workers can gain the trust of all parties. In recent years, all industries have been depressed, and many are strong on the outside but weak on the inside, so fundraising is even more difficult, but given the extent of the disaster area and the severity of the disaster, where will the funds come from, this has to depend on the fundraising of all parties, the source of the funds, no more than

(1) Central allocation | Like the old days of using regular items to issue inner treasury funds.

(2) Provincial treasury allocation | Allocation of provincial taxes and issuance of public bonds, etc.

(3) Local public funds | This includes county funds and all local public funds and public property.

(4) Mortgage loans | This is like the old days of diverting grain tribute for relief

(5) Fundraising for relief | This is obtained by soliciting donations from all walks of life.

These five sources need not be described too much. Only the (3) and (4) two types need to be slightly elaborated. Relief is best to be agile, three in the morning and four in the evening, indecision is not possible, and even migration delays are not possible. Therefore, fundraising for disaster relief, only those with personal interests, or witnessing the depth of the disaster, can work hard. Therefore, the center of disaster relief should focus on the disaster-stricken county. The county's financial resources are not sufficient, so please help from all sides. And should first use its existing to provide relief. Now that all parties are having difficulties, the county treasury does not have much money, so it should use local public funds and public property. Local public funds and public property are concentrated in one place, but many are also distributed to all parties. The so-called distributed, distributed to the hands of local gentlemen. Many local public funds and public property were originally used for a certain undertaking, and later the undertaking was stopped, and the funds and property were nominally retained, with the spirit of not returning for a thousand years and not relying on them for ten thousand years, in fact, it is no different from encroachment. By the time years pass and months pass, the local people do not know about this, then it becomes their private property, and people consider them to be wealthy gentry, and those who know it do not want to ask. These things are common in counties and towns. Now, in the time of heavy disaster and people's difficulties, regardless of what kind of public funds and public property, they should be ordered to hand them over, concentrate them for disaster relief, and those who conceal them will be allowed to be reported, and those who report them will be rewarded. If they can be gathered in one place, the number will definitely be considerable. If the public property cannot be immediately converted into money, fortunately there are banks everywhere. It is with [going to the countryside] as their popular slogan, you may want to mortgage loans to them to fill the relief, just like the old days of diverting grain tribute to save the disaster, now there is no grain tribute to divert, but if there were grain tributes in the counties, there is no name for grain tribute, but there is still its reality, so no matter whether it is to change the name, or to merge with other items, in short, there is the element of grain tribute in it. At this moment, waiting for top relief, is like longing for rain in a long drought, not knowing when to get it, even if relief is obtained, investigation, compilation, reporting, review, approval, allocation, distribution, and allocation of funds, to get to the disaster victims, do not know what year and what month? Those who live in high places, can know the depth of the disaster of the people, do not want them to have actions that disrupt order, such as robbing rice, sitting in large households, demanding food, causing trouble · · · · · · also can not bear their haggard to the point of death, such as exile, starvation, suicide by poisoning, or suffocation to death; also can not bear to see their parents and children separated, selling children and daughters; and for a time can not immediately raise huge funds to provide relief, then why not allow the counties to leave a year or two in the grain tributes that should be paid (this year's field tax, of course, to be exempted, after next year's harvest, can be collected), and in the conditional review of the loan conditions, the counties can borrow on their own, to save the dying disaster victims, it is also not a method, now what is used to provide disaster relief, mostly focus on leveling the rice price, followed by leveling the rice sale, even if the rice price is level, (how to level the price is still a problem) leveling the rice sale has been done, in the rural bankruptcy serious drought environment, disaster victims are mostly unable to buy, still have no food to eat, to starve to death. The second is to organize work relief, work relief is again in the investigation and measurement; and even if it is held, and the work is not in the disaster area, whether to immigrate to take the work? Furthermore, after a major disaster, there is always a major epidemic. This year's drought has been too long, rivers are dry, drinking water is very difficult, taking water only exists in the desolate water of ponds, many dig mud to find water, drilling wells to find springs. Taking drinks here, washing here, accumulation of dirt, must reach. Fortunately, although there are many dysentery symptoms, there is no major epidemic; but there are more and more patients, and how can we know if it will not spread for a long time? Thinking about the future and preventing it is also an action that should be taken in disaster relief.

The disaster is deep! Autumn harvest is hopeless, the future is long, and the disaster victims are wandering in the realm of life and death. The seasons are changing. Autumn goes to winter, and they point to ask about things, no clothes and no coarse clothes, how to end the year! What's more, there is no food? This is deeply hoped that all circles will send a mournful heart and start relief together. Especially hoping that those with responsibilities will think of the skin is gone, the hair is attached, hunger and blockage give birth to thieving hearts; if they all rise up and [eat begging rice], and shout [starving to death], then it is not easy to remedy, so this is not the time for grandstanding; the key is to quickly catch up and rescue the people from the mire.

The Necessary Understanding of the Issue of Silver Exportation by Wei Youpei 208

The issue of silver exportation has, in recent days, garnered quite a bit of attention from society. There are numerous critics, discussants, and those attempting to prevent its outflow, and some overly assertive arguments may cause public anxiety. In reality, silver exportation didn't start today, although it is more pronounced today, it has never been a focus of attention. Therefore, before discussing this issue, I feel it's important to focus not on the immediate, temporary problem, but on the long-term, permanent one.

Regarding the current silver outflow issue, some scholars believe that the solution lies in managing the trade deficit. This theory is correct in principle, but the current silver outflow cannot be attributed solely to the trade deficit. This is because the international trade deficit is not a recent phenomenon, but a constant in trade history for decades. The deficit in the past seven months has been decreasing due to declining domestic purchasing power. The total trade deficit for the seven months was over 32.9 million, which is far less than the exported silver. Therefore, based on the historical trade deficit, the amount that should have been exported to balance international payments should be more than that. However, the current exports from Shanghai are only about one-third of the trade deficit.

From the perspective of those engaged in exportation, most are foreign banks. Foreign businesses generally do not deposit their earnings from international trade in Chinese banks. As a result of the trade deficit, large amounts of silver flow into foreign banks every day. If all the silver held this year and in previous years were to be exported, the total would certainly not exceed 100 million.

The silver that has flowed into foreign banks over the years is, in reality, the same as being exported. The only difference is that one is stored in Shanghai and the other is stored abroad. The current exports are merely due to the desire to profit from the exchange rate difference. This silver is being transported from Shanghai back to foreign countries, and has long been isolated from the Chinese market, so its export has no direct impact on China's financial market.

Of course, it must be acknowledged that not all of the exported silver belongs to foreign banks. Some is entrusted by speculative merchants. Why would speculative merchants entrust its exportation? Naturally, it's because the exchange rate between domestic and foreign silver prices offers a profit opportunity. What worries us is this speculative activity. Because silver exportation due to the trade deficit is predictable, but these speculators will continue exporting as long as the exchange rate is not balanced. Therefore, even if the trade deficit is managed and reduced, these speculators cannot be eliminated. Therefore, to stop silver outflow, the solution lies only in managing silver prices, not in addressing the trade deficit.

Furthermore, silver exportation does not cause a major panic in Shanghai's financial market. The public's excessive concern that Shanghai's finances will gradually dry up is, at least, not currently the case. Looking at the Shanghai financial market's interbank loan rates in recent months, the average rate in June was 6%, and in July it was also 6%. From August 1st to 16th, it was 7%, and from the 17th to the 19th, it was 8%, showing a gradual upward trend. From the 20th to the 26th, a fluctuating trend can be observed:

August 20th: 10% August 24th: 15%

August 21st: 11% August 25th: 10%

August 22nd: 13% August 26th: 7%

August 23rd: 13%

Although an interbank loan rate of 10% is the highest seen this year, the 15% on August 24th was the highest peak this year. But compared to normal years, the market does not consider this a serious situation. The rise starting on the 21st had a special cause: the collapse of the Wu Hua Industrial Bank, which caused aftershocks of panic. As for the sudden rise on the 24th, it was purely due to the newspapers printing the silver export issue in large headlines, which stirred up public sentiment. Therefore, from the 25th onwards, the rates gradually declined. The fact that the market has not been severely affected during this period of reduced reserves is due to the circulation of paper currency.

Balancing international trade payments can certainly reduce silver outflow, but the current focus should be on how to raise domestic silver prices and stop speculation. Otherwise, even with a trade surplus, silver outflow may still not be stopped. Although large-scale silver outflow may not have an immediate impact on Shanghai's finances, speculation will eventually affect silver reserves. According to the effect of exchange rates, if there is a difference in exchange rates between two locations, buying and selling will equalize the prices. However, as long as the global currency war continues, exchange rate differences will never be balanced. Therefore, finding a way to raise domestic silver prices becomes the central issue.

Report on the Inspection of New Coins in August 210

丨丨Repair and Suspension of Minting in July丨丨

In August of this year, the Central Mint submitted 5.9 million yuan of new coins minted in the 23rd year (of the Republic) for inspection. The inspection committee of the mint appointed assayer Ge Laide (transliteration) to conduct random inspections according to regulations. The fineness and weight were in accordance with the Silver Standard Coinage Regulations. Certificates were issued from number (23) 2386 to number (23) 3423, totaling 1,038 certificates. In addition, the Central Mint produced 4,827 Grade B mint bars (880 fineness) in August, from number 26491 to number 31317. The calibration marks were also supervised and stamped according to regulations. Due to the repair of machinery and the refining of dust in July, the minting of new coins and bars was suspended in that month, and there were no products. This has been announced by the Inspection Committee of the Mint.
