Shen Bao Medical and Pharmaceutical Weekly

Excerpt on Typhoid Fever 4 (Taiyang) (Part 1) 220

— Yu Yunxiu

The Treatise on Cold Damage, Debating Pulse Diagnosis, says: [The pulse is floating and tight. Floating indicates wind. Tight indicates cold. Wind injures the Wei (defensive qi). Cold injures the Rong (nutritive qi). When both Rong and Wei are injured, the bones and joints become painful and restless. One should induce sweating.] This is the foundation upon which the Taiyang chapter is based. Zhu Fengyi said: [Guizhi Decoction is mainly for injuring the Wei. Mahuang Decoction is mainly for injuring the Rong. Major Green Dragon Decoction is for injuring both Rong and Wei.] This is the beginning of the three fundamental principles of the Taiyang chapter. Later, Xu Xue Shi followed this. Until Fang Zhonghang's Annotations on the Treatise on Cold Damage, the Taiyang chapter was divided into three parts: upper, middle, and lower. Wind injuring the Wei was designated as the upper part, cold injuring the Rong as the middle part, and wind and cold injuring both Rong and Wei as the lower part. Yu Jiayan adopted this theory and wrote the Shang Lun chapter. Wei Litong followed this and wrote The Original Meaning of the Treatise on Cold Damage. Those who discuss the Treatise on Cold Damage later mostly treat the three fundamental principles of wind injuring the Wei, cold injuring the Rong, and wind and cold injuring both Rong and Wei as immutable. To understand the fallacy of this, one must begin by understanding the Rong and Wei themselves.

The Spiritual Pivot, Chapter on the Meeting of Nutritive and Defensive Qi, says: [The clear is the nutritive (qi), the turbid is the defensive (qi). The nutritive (qi) is within the vessels, the defensive (qi) is outside the vessels.] It also says: [The nutritive (qi) originates from the middle Jiao (burner), the defensive (qi) originates from the lower Jiao (burner).] It also says: [The middle Jiao also comes from the stomach and goes to the upper Jiao. It separates the dregs, steams the fluids, and transforms them into their essence. It ascends to the lung vessels, where it transforms into blood to nourish the body. Nothing is more important than this. Therefore, it is only able to travel through the meridians and is called the nutritive qi.] From this perspective, the nutritive (qi) is blood. Blood congeals when it encounters cold, as is the case with frostbite. Therefore, the theory of cold injuring the nutritive (qi) seems to be well-founded. However, frostbite is completely different from the Taiyang chapter of cold damage. If one wants to force an analogy, frostbite is not without symptoms of tight pulse and aversion to cold. However, additional symptoms such as drowsiness and staggering gait are not found in Taiyang cold damage. Furthermore, it can only occur when the air temperature drops below negative ten degrees Celsius, and it is extremely rare in the south. How can it be as Zhongjing (Zhang Zhongjing) said, that two-thirds of the clan die from this disease? It must be as Qin Huangzhu said, that Zhongjing was a native of Nanyang, Hebei, and cold damage is a disease of the northern winter months before it can be forced. However, Shi Busi has already refuted Qin's theory. Therefore, frostbite and Taiyang cold damage are as unrelated as a horse and a cow. It is clear that Taiyang cold damage is not cold injuring the Rong.

As for the Wei, we still do not know what it is. Judging from the Internal Classic's theory that the turbid is the Wei, then it is a useless waste product in the body. Judging from the theory that the Wei originates from the lower Jiao, it is the urine of the bladder. The Spiritual Pivot, Chapter on the Meeting of Nutritive and Defensive Qi, says: [The lower Jiao separates the large and small intestines, pours into the bladder, and seeps into it.] This is my evidence that the Wei is urine. Urine is a waste product in the body, which is consistent with the theory that the turbid is the Wei. Furthermore, judging from the theory that the Wei travels outside the vessels, the network of pathways in the human body that is similar to blood vessels is the nervous system and the lymphatic vessels. However, the nervous system cannot be said to be turbid, and injury to the nervous system will inevitably cause pain and paralysis, which is not present in Taiyang cold damage. Therefore, it can be determined that the Wei is not the nervous system. Then the Wei is the lymphatic system. What is lymph? In a broad sense, it is the fluid outside the blood vessels. All fluids between tissue cells that are not surrounded by blood vessels and do not travel within the meridians can be called lymph. The fluid in the cerebrospinal canal and the fluid in the pericardium are also included. However, these two cannot be said to be turbid, and injury to these two will inevitably cause symptoms of meningitis and pericarditis. The changes in these fluids are actually affected by meningitis and pericarditis, placing them in a passive position and unable to cause disease on their own. Therefore, the so-called Wei is not lymph in the broad sense. Then the Wei is the lymph in the narrow sense, which is the lymph fluid in the tissue cells and lymphatic vessels.

Lymph is filled in the gaps between tissue cells and serves as a medium for metabolism between blood and tissue cells. Its origin is still from the blood vessels. Liquid leaks from the capillary vessels and enters between the tissue cells, which is lymph. Therefore, the composition of lymph is roughly the same as that of plasma, and it is not particularly different from blood. Lymph from the tissue cells comes from the blood and is then reabsorbed by the blood vessels. The remaining sediment that is not absorbed flows into the small lymphatic vessels distributed between the tissue cells. The small lymphatic vessels flow into the large lymphatic vessels, and the large lymphatic vessels flow into the large venous vessels, where they mix with the blood again. Lymph comes from the blood vessels, carrying nutrients. When it returns to the blood vessels and flows into the small lymphatic vessels in other directions, it carries waste products away, which is what is meant by turbid. However, as a result, a part of it still returns to the blood vessels, and although a part of it passes through the lymphatic vessels, it eventually enters the blood vessels. Therefore, an injury to this is an injury to the nutritive blood. How can it be separated from the injury to the nutritive blood and exist independently?

Murder by Incompetent Doctors 221

— Song Guobin

Only incompetent doctors commit murder,

Good doctors uphold morality and cherish benevolence.

May the court not heed false accusations,

So that medical disputes may cease.

The world declines, and people's hearts become more treacherous. Medical disputes are increasing daily, and appearing in court has become commonplace. However, upon closer examination, regardless of the facts, patients accuse doctors of "murder by incompetent doctors." To call a doctor incompetent implies that their knowledge and character are insufficient for their profession, and thus, their killing is understandable. However, it is unreasonable to suspect a doctor who is not incompetent, whose knowledge is recognized by schools, whose qualifications are recognized by the state, and whose credibility is recognized by society, of deliberately committing murder. Therefore, licensed doctors would never commit murder, while incompetent doctors inevitably would. Are all those currently accused by patients truly incompetent doctors? As seen in the conclusion of many cases, the medical professionals often win, indicating that the accused are not incompetent doctors but are innocent victims. Therefore, when the court receives such cases, it should first investigate thoroughly. If the accused is a licensed doctor, the case should be dismissed because licensed doctors cannot be legitimately accused.

Let me explain the reasons why licensed doctors cannot be accused:

(1) Licensed doctors, having graduated from formal medical schools and received advanced education, possess considerable character and knowledge and would never engage in exaggeration or deception. They do not rely on advertisements to attract patients; patients come naturally. Confucius said: "The superior man learns to attain his Dao." Licensed doctors are the same, learning to attract patients; they come without being sought. If the outcome is unsatisfactory, the responsibility should not fall solely on the doctor. However, it is different for quack doctors, who exaggerate in their advertisements and offer low consultation fees. Patients come because they are misled by the advertisements and are not acting on their own volition. Therefore, if there are errors, quack doctors should bear legal responsibility, and the court should impose severe penalties.

(2) Licensed doctors possess ample knowledge and rich experience, and patients should absolutely obey them. Their diagnoses and treatments are beyond the understanding of patients. Medical conditions are constantly changing, and doctors cannot cure all diseases. It is unfounded for patients with no medical knowledge to claim that the doctor's diagnosis is inaccurate or the treatment is wrong. Even if other doctors are consulted, their conjectures after the fact cannot be as accurate as the observations of the original treating physician. Therefore, for patients to question the appropriateness of a doctor's diagnosis and treatment as grounds for litigation is like a summer insect talking about ice, pretending to know what they do not. As for quack doctors, who lack knowledge, their diagnoses and treatments are often erroneous. Occasional cures are due to luck, and failures are undoubtedly due to mistakes. Patients should certainly accuse and sue them, unlike licensed doctors.

(3) Licensed doctors have earned their reputations over time. They approach diagnoses with extreme caution and never act negligently. Accusing doctors of intentional murder is absurd. Why would a doctor hate a patient enough to intentionally kill them? Why would a doctor hate their own hard-earned reputation enough to deliberately destroy it? This shows the absurdity of the accusation of intentional murder. Doctors treat diseases without intentional fault. Even if something unfortunate happens, it is unintentional, a matter of academic debate, not a legal one. Therefore, licensed doctors should not bear criminal responsibility. However, quack doctors, driven by profit, disregard morality and shame, performing abortions at will. Patients should not allow them to escape justice.

(4) Life is priceless. Licensed doctors save thousands of lives, and their contributions are evident to the world. Even if there are one or two unintentional errors, the merits outweigh the demerits. Public opinion should recognize this. Demands for civil compensation often use the deceased's financial value as the basis (e.g., demanding compensation of 10,000 yuan because the deceased could earn 1,000 yuan per year for ten more years). Then, shouldn't doctors also have the same demands for patients they have cured? Patients often begrudge paying doctors' fees but demand exorbitant sums upon death as leverage. Is this fair? Therefore, doctors should not be liable for civil damages. However, if such incidents occur with quack doctors who aim to make money, they should be fined heavily to curb their deceitful intentions and deter others.

(5) Doctors have the right to maintain the patient's privacy. They treat patients as their own responsibility. Except for formal consultations, no third parties should be involved. This is essential for responsible treatment, as seen in civilized and advanced countries. However, the situation is different in our country. Patients may consult different doctors, using both modern and traditional medicine, mixing Chinese and Western treatments. These situations are difficult to describe in detail. When the condition changes, they want the modern doctor to bear full responsibility. How can that responsibility be assigned? Therefore, modern doctors in China today cannot bear any legal responsibility. Yet, they are constantly being accused, which is unfair.

In summary, medical disputes have many causes, and the court's readiness to accept cases encourages patients to litigate. The key is for the court to investigate whether the accused is a licensed doctor before accepting the case. If the accused is a licensed doctor, the lawsuit should be rejected. This will eliminate false accusations, resolve disputes, and protect the medical profession. This is what I hope for!

Protecting Children's Teeth (Part 2) 222

— Lin Jianxian

Protect the First Permanent Molars

From the chart above of the eruption times of permanent teeth, we can see that the first molars erupt between the ages of five and seven. These teeth are the cornerstones of the dental arch. If these teeth are lost, the adjacent teeth are prone to tipping and becoming maloccluded. In adulthood, the chin recedes, the face loses its symmetry, and the teeth are misaligned and prone to decay. Parents often mistakenly think that these teeth are temporary baby teeth and allow them to decay, affecting all future teeth, which is a pity. Therefore, parents should always pay attention to the emergence of these teeth and protect them. Once these teeth erupt, other permanent teeth will erupt in succession.

How to Prevent Tooth Decay

The prevention of tooth decay can be summarized into the following four aspects:

(1) Develop Good Habits: Mothers should clean their infant's mouth with disinfectant solution daily before the teeth erupt. When the teeth first erupt, they should wipe off any debris with a clean, damp cloth. At four or five years old, children should be given a small toothbrush with soft, fine bristles and taught how to brush their teeth. This trains children to develop good oral hygiene habits. Once this habit is formed, they will maintain it throughout their lives, and their teeth will not easily decay. Therefore, developing good habits is the most effective way to prevent dental problems.

(2) Reasonable Brushing Method: First, soak the toothbrush in warm water, then apply toothpaste or tooth powder. When brushing, brush both the inside and outside surfaces, especially the inside. The brushing motion should be vertical or circular, so the debris in the gaps between teeth can be swept away. Many people brush horizontally or only brush the outside or front. This makes it difficult to remove debris and can cause dental problems.

Brush your teeth once every morning and after each meal. At a minimum, brush twice a day, once in the morning and once after dinner. Children like to eat sweets, but sugar easily turns into acid and damages tooth enamel. It is best to reduce snacking or brush immediately after eating to prevent food residue from harming the teeth.

(3) Choose Beneficial Foods: Food is essential for healthy teeth. Strong teeth are created by nutritious food. Mothers should choose foods rich in calcium during pregnancy, such as milk, eggs, vegetables, oranges, and brown rice (avoid over-processed white rice), to strengthen their children's teeth. During the growth period, children should eat foods rich in vitamins, such as egg yolks, milk, cod liver oil, oranges, and vegetables, as these are very beneficial to their teeth.

(4) Regular Dental Checkups: Children have baby teeth changing around the age of seven. During these seven years, it is best to have a dental checkup every six months. Treat any problems and remove plaque to prevent early loss of baby teeth. If a baby tooth feels loose, it should be removed immediately. Otherwise, permanent teeth may erupt from the front or back, causing misalignment. Even after all the permanent teeth come in, regular dental checkups and cleaning are still important.

Routine dental checkups and treatment are the most economical approach. For example, if person A gets regular dental checkups every year, and person B neglects their teeth, person A will have clean teeth and good oral health, while person B will suffer from dental problems. Because teeth decay, become infected, and require extraction, they may need dentures. The pain, money, and time spent are several times more than person A. Therefore, regular dental checkups are essential for preventing dental problems.

The Impact of Teeth on Physical Health

Everyone knows that food must be chewed thoroughly for easy digestion. If teeth are lost and proper chewing is impossible, the body will not be able to fully absorb and assimilate the food for nourishment. Eating twice as much food only yields half the benefits. Without proper digestion, how can one expect to be healthy?

Diseased teeth or decayed teeth with dead pulp can cause infectious foci, which reduce the body's resistance and lead to various diseases, such as sinusitis, pneumonia, arthritis, pleurisy, meningitis, pericarditis, periostitis, appendicitis, lung disease, deafness, and epilepsy. Many of these diseases are caused by pus from tooth decay flowing into the body through the blood vessels or esophagus. The mouth is the passageway for food. No matter how clean the food is, it cannot remain hygienic if it passes through a mouth full of decay, bacteria, and grime. Therefore, teeth are crucial to health.

The Contribution of Preventive Dentistry

The greatest contribution of dentistry to society is not in surgical dentistry or restorative dentistry, but in preventive dentistry. Preventive dentistry is the study of how to prevent dental diseases in humans. This is the most advanced and valuable field in dentistry. Scholars in various countries are focusing on this area. With the advancement of this field, humans will have healthy teeth, and the other two branches can be eliminated. American dentist Dr. Fones was a strong and long-time proponent of preventive dentistry. His patient records show that many of his former child patients have grown into young adults with beautiful smiles and healthy teeth, free of cavities and fillings, living healthy and happy lives.

Therefore, preventive dentistry does benefit society in reality. Dental professionals in various countries have long recognized the importance of children's oral hygiene, and parents are increasingly aware of it. Therefore, they can cooperate with dentists, seek advice regularly, and implement preventive measures, so their children can benefit for a lifetime. In our country, parents rarely take their children to the dentist unless they have a toothache. The reasons for this include: (1) lack of understanding of the importance of prevention; (2) saving on dental fees; (3) fear of children crying, which causes more trouble. (In fact, parents can give positive suggestions, so children know the dentist will not cause them pain, but will make their teeth beautiful and eliminate toothaches. Then, children will be happy to comply.) I dare to sincerely tell my fellow citizens that the spiritual, time, and monetary losses that children suffer from unhealthy teeth will be hundreds of times more than the current dental fees. Fellow citizens, rather than spending a lot of effort to treat adults, why not spend less effort to raise healthy children?

A Brief Discussion on Pulmonary Tuberculosis (19) 223

— Hu Jiayan

The onset of pulmonary tuberculosis is mostly insidious; its course is also very chronic, lasting not only three or five years, but also twenty or thirty years. Besides this, it can also begin acutely, but this is relatively rare. In this case, the temperature will suddenly increase at the beginning, accompanied by subjective symptoms such as headache and limb pain; this situation is very similar to the flu. If we conduct a thorough examination, there is nothing to find in the auscultation and percussion, but tuberculosis bacteria can be found in the morning sputum, and X-rays can reveal the infiltration.

Among the acute onsets of this disease, the most prominent is caseous pneumonia! It is suddenly triggered by a high fever and a state of general lethargy, and most cases are incurable; this appearance is almost the same as acute infectious diseases. In addition, there is a type where the lesion is not caseous pneumonia, but its spread is very rapid, and the appearance is similar; this is the ordinary [galloping consumption]. The course of these two types is completely different from the previous chronic type; their prognosis is very poor, and even general physicians are afraid of them.

The onset of pulmonary tuberculosis has already been discussed above. Regarding its general important symptoms, such as night sweats, cough, hemoptysis, dyspnea, temperature, etc., I will now describe them one by one below:

(1) Night sweats: Most common tuberculosis patients experience increased temperature at night, and excessive sweating occurs when their temperature drops in the middle of the night or early morning. This symptom can disrupt the patient's sleep and consume their physical strength. In addition, it can also occur in the early stages of the disease; experienced physicians will not easily overlook it. However, we must know that nervous causes such as insomnia, mental disturbance, and frequent dreams due to overstimulation can also cause it. These should not be confused.

(2) Weight Loss: This is a warning to the patient. If ordinary people gradually lose weight for no reason, although it cannot be said to be definitely pulmonary tuberculosis, at least it can be said that a thorough lung examination is inevitable. The reason for this is probably due to poor appetite and weight loss; the rise in material exchange function is inevitably related. This is not to mention for patients who usually have a fever, but there are also more than 30% of such cases without a temperature increase phenomenon. The occurrence of this symptom does not mean that the disease has worsened. In fact, what the facts tell us is sometimes the opposite: in people with good nutritional status, their lung damage is easily enlarged; and the disease suffered by the weak is mostly more likely to develop induration, and the prognosis is better.

(3) Anemia: Ordinary people suffering from this disease always have a pale color: if the patient is a woman, it is easy to confuse it with chlorosis. But the fact is not always the case. It is true that the number of red blood cells and hemoglobin components in patients with this disease can sometimes be reduced, just like chlorosis; but most of it is so when the disease is progressing, and there is no such significant change usually. The same is true for the increase in the number of blood cells and lymphatic leukocytes. The differentiation of these two aspects, of course, requires a precise blood test before it can be revealed. The details of the matter can only be described in another chapter on clinical examination methods!

(4) Cough: Cough is one of the important symptoms of pulmonary tuberculosis, and the sentence "prolonged cough is easy to become consumption" has almost become a common saying. When we diagnose diseases, many patients who come to see us because of a cough end up developing tuberculous lesions; even the patients themselves sometimes feel that they have been coughing for too long and are afraid of tuberculous causes. Among them, there are also many people who have not sought medical attention. From this situation, we can know that the general public attaches great importance to this symptom. At the beginning of this disease, many people do not cough, and even if they do, most of it is related to external attacks, such as dust, coal ash, and prolonged loud talking, which are generally unrelated to tuberculosis itself. When it develops into a dry cough, even a spasmodic cough, it is mostly caused by dry pleurisy or laryngitis. Coughing in pulmonary tuberculosis itself is mostly due to sputum remaining in the trachea; we know that there is a kind of cilia in the trachea, which is dedicated to sputum discharge. In this case, the patient certainly has to cough. In this case, many patients have no interruption, but some people have severe coughs every morning and evening. In addition, one thing should also be mentioned, that is: sometimes there is no cough at all when the disease progresses. Of course, this is very rare. The author remembers that he once diagnosed a patient who had a lot of tuberculosis bacteria in his sputum, which was undoubtedly open pulmonary tuberculosis; in the X-ray examination, except for a part of the lower lobe, almost the entire lung was initially infiltrated. This situation, of course, is very serious, but he has no cough symptoms at all. Based on this point, readers can imagine how complicated and atypical the symptoms of pulmonary tuberculosis are.

Random Notes on Vaccination (Continued) 224

— Zang Hebai

Also, the current practitioners who advertise using the "old method of cowpox vaccination" do not preserve the national essence: they do not use human lymph, but use the cowpox vaccine used by us. The only difference is that they vaccinate more times on both arms. You should know that the immunity obtained after vaccination can be achieved with one or ten inoculations. There is no difference in their degree. Although there is something morally questionable about these old-fashioned smallpox practitioners using cowpox vaccine, I especially welcome it in fact. Why? Because cowpox vaccine is disinfected. If it has not passed its effective time, it can be used boldly without harm. Human lymph is difficult to ask about. However, I feel that in addition to using cowpox vaccine, why not use general disinfection methods, which would be even better?

During vaccination, there are also two things that are often encountered in society: "eating triggering foods" and "abstaining from certain foods." Old-fashioned smallpox practitioners also think these are very important. In fact, the production and disappearance of immunity has absolutely nothing to do with dietary intake. If it does, there is no need to promote flower-like immunity by eating some triggering foods! Do people who abstain from certain foods very strictly never lose their smallpox immunity? And the facts tell us that after vaccination, eating whatever you want, not eating triggering foods beforehand, and not abstaining from certain foods afterward, does not mean that the immunity in the body has disappeared. There is no difference between the first and second vaccinations.

Red light has been found to be beneficial to natural smallpox (i.e., human smallpox rash) based on experience, but it has no effect on artificial smallpox (i.e., the vaccinated smallpox)! And the general public in society puts many red cloths around the heads of vaccinated children, calling it "wearing red," and also wears red shirts and pants, which is unnecessary.

Most of us know that the only way to prevent smallpox is by vaccination. I don't know what use it is to paste strips of red paper a few inches wide and three or four inches long with the words "smallpox has passed" on the doors of every house in an area where smallpox is prevalent, and to attach similar red cloth strips to children. Even if we say that red light is the only weapon to kill smallpox pathogens (which have not yet been discovered), let's close our eyes and think: Can such a large house and such a large child be isolated from the elusive smallpox pathogens with such a large paper strip or cloth strip? Is the operation so simple? Can the desired goal be achieved?

When vaccinating, the general public welcomes vaccination practitioners to vaccinate their children until they bleed, which is incorrect! Because when we vaccinate, we only need to cut through the thinnest layer of epidermis and let the applied vaccine be absorbed through the opening. The vaccine can enter through the opening. At that time, the opening must be able to have an absorptive effect. Scientifically speaking, that place must have a negative pressure. If that place is bleeding, it is not an absorptive effect, but a breathing effect, which is a positive pressure. Doesn't this go against the original intention of applying the vaccine?

The four seasons of spring, summer, autumn and winter have nothing to do with vaccination. However, because the weather is hot in summer, the effectiveness of the vaccine is easily lost; the weather is cold in winter, and people who are vaccinated are prone to catch a cold. The climate in spring and autumn is neither cold nor warm, and there are no such disadvantages, so it is suitable. It is also wrong for society to only believe in vaccinating in spring and not in autumn!

Babies can be vaccinated as early as eighty days after birth. Also, when smallpox is very prevalent, they should be vaccinated as early as seven days after they are born. It is even more unreasonable for the general public to say that babies' internal organs are not fully developed and that they can only be vaccinated after one or two years old! Because babies' internal organs are fully equipped at birth, and what is the relationship between the production of smallpox immunity and whether the five internal organs are complete?

Common Sense of Hygiene for Ears, Nose, Throat, and Eyes (13) 225

— Tang Renjin

(13) Peritonsillar Inflammation and Peritonsillar Abscess

This disease occurs when suffering from lacunar tonsillitis. If, after the body temperature drops and local pain subsides, sudden chills and shivering occur, and the fever rises again, the patient feels particularly severe pain in the tonsillar region on the affected side (mostly limited to one side; it rarely occurs on both sides). The pain can often radiate to the ear. Swallowing becomes very difficult. During meals, liquids often flow backward and out through the nasal cavity. If the pain becomes more intense, swallowing becomes completely impossible. Even swallowing a few drops of water is considered a painful event by the patient. The patient's mental state is very sensitive and easily angered. Sleep at night is also restless, and speech is inconvenient. When the doctor examines the throat, the patient is often unwilling to open their mouth due to the difficulty of opening it and the pain. If they reluctantly endure the pain and open their mouth, or if an oral retractor is used, the soft palate on the affected side is seen to be highly red and swollen, sometimes involving the soft palate. The palatine tonsil is also clearly congested. If a probe is used to touch the swollen area, it feels hard and resistant, and the patient feels tenderness. This is called peritonsillitis. If these symptoms persist for one or two days, the swollen area may soften and become fluctuating. This is due to the formation of pus. At this time, it is called peritonsillar abscess. The patient suffers the most at this time, full of self-pity and resentment, unable to sit or lie still. The head and neck are often tilted. The area near the abscess often shows inflammatory swelling. The uvula and the soft palate on the healthy side are also often swollen.

Speaking of the treatment methods for this disease, it is best to implement appropriate treatment when suffering from lacunar tonsillitis to prevent the occurrence of peritonsillar inflammation early on. Once peritonsillar inflammation has occurred, drug application, gargling, and covering methods should be continued repeatedly. If the pain is unbearable and there are already fluctuations, then surgery must be performed to incise and drain the pus. The pain can then stop on its own, and the patient will immediately feel relief. After two or three days, they can fully recover and regain their health.

Little Western Heaven 226

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 1: A Ghost Carries a Carriage of Distant Guests from Guanzhong, A Poor Family Crosses the Ferry, Mourning a Qin Man

He took the duster and swatted it all over his body, stirring up a cloud of smoke and dust, a layer of gray in the white light. At this time, a man in a Western suit was standing under the eaves of the house, just looking at them. Seeing the tea boy carrying a basin of water to this room, he smiled and said, "Your business is really good, this row of houses in the back is full again today." Li Shilian heard his accent, which was also Southern, clearly a guest as well. He felt like he was in a foreign land, and the principle of [bowing to every Buddha encountered] was most applicable. As an official, as long as you know more friends, there's always a way. So he took this opportunity and interjected, "The hotel business is so good in Xi'an." As he spoke, he smiled and nodded to the man. The man naturally couldn't accept it so casually, so he nodded back. Li Shilian then took another step forward, bowing and smiling, "This gentleman also has a Southern accent, what is your honorable surname?" Seeing him so polite, the man couldn't refuse too much, so he smiled and said he was from Jiangsu, named Cheng Zhiqian, and had come here to investigate education, as he was a teacher at a middle school. Li Shilian heard that he was here to investigate education, and whether or not he connected with this kind of person didn't matter much to him. So the conversation ended there. He went back into his room to pack his luggage and no longer tried to make friends with Cheng Zhiqian. By this time, it was already after four o'clock in the afternoon. He washed his face and asked the hotel for something to eat, and the sky was already getting dark. But the first thing that made him unhappy was that the tea boy brought in a tall kerosene lamp in the dim light. When the lamp was placed on the table, the white walls of the room seemed to take on a yellowish hue. Li Shilian was thirty-six years old this year, and since he was twenty, he had never lived with an oil lamp. Now, suddenly seeing it, he couldn't say exactly what kind of boredom he felt in his heart. He was feeling very bored. (10)

Nameless Heroes 227

— Li Kui

These anti-Japanese heroes are not as famous as Ma Zhanshan and Cai Tingkai; that's why they are called nameless heroes.

But their bravery, their spirit of sacrifice, is truly more worthy of admiration than those famous heroes.

I will now tell this story: It was after the September 18th Incident, when Japan had already occupied Liaoning, Jilin, and part of Heilongjiang, but had not yet occupied Harbin.

When the Japanese attacked Harbin, Ding Chao's troops resisted; so there was a very fierce battle in Majiagou.

After fighting for a day and a night, Ding Chao's troops were finally defeated! Because Japan had planes dropping bombs in the sky, and tanks charging forward on the ground! Their military equipment was very pitiful, without anti-aircraft guns or trenches; so they were only retreating step by step.

However, some soldiers had been chased and couldn't run away, and were about to die under machine-gun fire! Seeing that running was also death, they immediately turned around and fought the enemy to the death! Some lay horizontally in front of the tanks to stop them from advancing; some used their bayonets to thrust into the gun holes.

At this time, half of them were killed again, but they still desperately fought the enemy hand-to-hand! Finally, they killed the enemies inside the tanks and captured these tanks.

These anti-Japanese heroes are truly admirable and can be remembered in the history of the anti-Japanese war; but they are nameless heroes!

I think the reason they are nameless is because their achievements are built on their own blood, not on the skulls of others.

New Incantation for Begging for Rain 229

— Sha Ou

Chinese farmers who rely on the heavens for their livelihoods have already gazed with longing eyes in this year of drought and heat. The gods of the Five Sacred Mountains and Four Great Rivers, famous mountains and great rivers, have completely lost their efficacy. News of reporting famine, fleeing famine, begging for relief, and robbing rice fills the pages of newspapers. Artificial rainmaking using scientific methods is still a distant water that cannot quench the immediate thirst. In a situation where nothing can be done, performing old tricks such as setting up altars, building altars, banning slaughter, and praying for rain is only a case of calling upon the heavens without response and summoning the earth without result, a consolation that is better than nothing.

In the Song Dynasty, there was a so-called lizard rain-making method, where live lizards were caught and placed in urns, and twenty-eight boy children, with their faces, hands, and feet painted blue, holding willow branches and sprinkling water, circled around chanting incantations. Although the ritual was ridiculous, the incantations were quite authentic. The incantation said:

[Lizard, lizard! Raise clouds and spit mist, make rain torrential, and let you return to the clouds.]

Records of Lingering Fragrance 230

— Originally Written by Princess Deling of the Qing Dynasty, Translated by Qin Shouou

If someone's ancestral graves happen to be near the railway, then these days, because they know that the Empress Dowager will be passing by here soon, they definitely won't dare to come to sweep the tombs. But when we look out from the car windows, we can still see them very clearly: they all turn their backs and dare not look us directly in the eye, because the local officials have already widely warned them. However, I can say with certainty: they did not comply with this secret order! Originally, curiosity is something that everyone must have. The common people only hear people talk about the Emperor and the Empress Dowager all year round, but they have never seen what kind of gods or people the Emperor or the Empress Dowager actually are. It is rare to encounter our special train, carrying the Empress Dowager and the Emperor, passing in front of them, so of course they would not want to miss this opportunity again. So they borrowed the posture of kneeling and worshiping the ancestral graves, lowered their heads, widened their eyes, and tried their best to peek from under their arms: however, at most they can only see this yellow train and many shadows of people squirming on the train. The true appearance of the Empress Dowager and the Emperor is still invisible.

Regarding the custom of sweeping tombs during Qingming, I also had a very memorable discussion with the Empress Dowager, and we both had the same feelings. If I were to record it, it would be another very long article.

Along the road we passed, almost all were tombs, so on this day, the people sweeping the tombs were indeed coming and going in an endless stream. The Empress Dowager gazed at them very attentively from the car window; at the same time, her face showed a layer of thoughtful, deep gray, and her eyebrows were also knitted together. Whenever she was pondering something, her attitude was always very melancholy and depressed. At this time, no matter what interesting thing happened, she would never laugh. (119)

Under our lower-class masses' philosophy of [Pantheism], the deities who bring rain and the techniques for seeking rain are fundamentally inexhaustible. The following chapters, imitating the ancients in a clumsy way, present rain-seeking incantations, although carrying some impertinent tone of questioning, can also represent the emotions of the lower people's resentment and anxiety:

Not a single cloud forms, not a drop of rain falls, the sun shines brightly all morning, a clear sky in broad daylight. (Chapter 1)

Thunder Rain Thunder Ancestor! Where have you retreated to? Could it be that you are being passive, the Electric Mother has lost her love. (Chapter 2)

In the past, Shang Tang cut his nails and hair, prayed for rain in Sanglin, and pretended to commit suicide, which also moved the heavens, and the rain poured down: Moreover, today's morning people are not lacking in hanging themselves!

The Blue-clad Daoists and the priests of the Yu Gate dance together, singing the Cloud Han, saying to bring rain. Now on the sea, dancing halls are everywhere, in jazz songs, swaying morning and night, the art of dancing is so skillful, why doesn't it rain? Cloud or rain, Om Mani Padme Hum! (Chapter 4)

Crickets 231

— Yan Bokuang

In the new autumn weather, the autumn insects in the fields chirp noisily. Children pick bricks and pull grass, searching hard, and at night they take flashlights or light red candles. If they are in deep holes, they pour cold water in to make them unable to hide and jump out. The children are quick-eyed and quick-handed, using small lead wire covers to cage them and catch them into tile pots.

When they are happy, they make an appointment with a friend, and each takes out a tile pot, puts the two crickets in a pot, baring their teeth and waving their claws, fighting each other, killing each other. The winner struts around, showing off his heroism, drumming his wings and chirping loudly, making his friend clap his hands and laugh.

Writing this, I remembered an interesting thing. In my hometown, two young men were pursuing the same girl, but the girl's marriage was in between, either one would be fine, because both young men were eagerly asking her who she belonged to. She was so anxious that she didn't know which one to agree to. Fortunately, she had a quick wit and said, "You two bring crickets to compete! See who wins?" At that time, it was already deep autumn weather. B spent five hundred yuan to buy a general who had been on the battlefield, and A also selected a brave hero. They invited witnesses and judges. In a great battle, in the end, she belonged to B. A was so angry that his body trembled, and he even dropped the tile pot hero on the ground.

The sound of insects on an autumn night is very desolate, like the sound of heavy rain in autumn echoing in the empty sky. The Chinese do not unite to resist foreign insults, but kill each other, truly like a pair of autumn insects.

Rambling Talk

Pleasure Boat 232

— Nangongsheng

A pleasure boat is a small boat for touring a lake, arranged very elegantly, very different from ordinary cargo ships that carry goods. Because this kind of pleasure boat is mostly in famous places with many waterways in lakes and islets, it is specially used for tourists to play in the scenery of the watery countryside, so the arrangement on the boat does not need to be practical, as long as it is exquisite, elegant, and suits the mood of the tourists.

The scenery and the clear beauty of the mountains and waters in various parts of China are no less than those of Switzerland, the world's park, especially in the watery countryside, which can be called a separate world. Boating in a small boat, one feels that all sorrows are washed away, and the body and mind are unusually relaxed and happy. Pleasure boats have been discovered in the watery countryside of various places due to this need. So, such places as Suzhou and Wuxi, which resemble Venice, the water city of Italy, can be seen everywhere with clear, green, and vast waves. No matter what famous place you go to, such as Xuanmu Mountain, Tianping Mountain, Tiger Hill, Shihu, Huiquan Mountain, Meiyuan, Taihu Lake, etc., the most convenient way is to travel by waterway, and pleasure boats have become the most suitable gift for tourists. In other scenic spots such as West Lake in Hangzhou, Slender West Lake in Yangzhou, and Daming Lake in Jinan, the most wonderful tourist areas are all in the green water and clear waves, and naturally pleasure boats have become a necessary item. Therefore, in these scenic spots, you can see three or five friends floating and sinking in a beautiful pleasure boat, drifting in the middle of the stream, their joy is harmonious, making you feel unparalleled admiration. However, the arrangement and style of pleasure boats in various places are completely different due to the size of the waterways and the different environments.

The pleasure boats in Suzhou must sail in the wide and deep Xujiang River, so they are larger than other places, except for Wuxi. The largest is more than ten zhang long, with an area of more than one zhang wide, divided into three parts: the bow, the stern, and the cabin. The large cabins are divided into three or two rooms, with exquisite and finely carved movable flower windows arranged on all sides. The whole boat is painted with bright and beautiful Guangqi original lacquer, and the couches, chairs, and tables in the cabin are all made of rosewood. There are two long oars on the stern, which are the only tools for sailing. The stove for cooking is also on the stern. There are only two stone steps on the bow to stabilize the center of gravity. The awning on top is also made of wood, and the bamboo pole for punting the boat is placed horizontally on top. The curtains for the cabin doors and windows are all made of very beautiful materials, so the whole boat meets the requirements of beauty and elegance.

The pleasure boats in Wuxi are similar to those in Suzhou, but they are slightly larger. This is because they have to go to the edge of Taihu Lake, so they have to be a little bigger. The interior arrangement is also the same as in Suzhou. The most famous thing on the boats, in both Suzhou and Wuxi, is the exquisite boat dish, which is still popular and praised today.

The pleasure boats in West Lake are different from those in Suzhou and Wuxi. The volume of the boat is small, with a snow-white cloth awning on the cabin, and some are surrounded by bronze railings, which is extraordinarily elegant. Wicker chairs and wicker tables are arranged in the cabin for tourists to sit and rest. There is only one wooden oar for sailing on the stern. On a clear night with a bright moon, sailing in the middle of the stream with two or three friends, this scene is truly better than the celestial beings in the sky. There are no dishes on the boat, but the famous ones are the clear spring and Longjing tea leaves of Hangzhou. The pleasure boats in Slender West Lake in Yangzhou are very similar to those in West Lake, but the boatmen who row the boats are mostly girls of fifteen or sixteen years old. The pleasure boats in these two places are only used for touring the lake and cannot sail in the deep rivers and pools like the pleasure boats in Suzhou and Wuxi, and they cannot be used as a place to rest.

The pleasure boats in Daming Lake are the strangest, without a bow, like a pleasure boat with the bow cut off. The awning of the cabin is made of a wooden frame with canvas. The interior arrangement is only wicker chairs and tables. There are no oars or paddles on the stern. The only thing for sailing is two tree trunks. Compared with the pleasure boats in Suzhou, Wuxi, and West Lake, the arrangement is the simplest. However, the pre-rain tea brewed with the water of Daming Lake can be compared with the water of Hupao and Longjing in West Lake, which is the most memorable thing.

In addition to the above places, there are also various types such as the Qinhuai pleasure boats, Jiangshan boats, and Guangzhou riverboats, but they are not only valued for their pleasure boats. Because all the boatmen on the boats are beautiful young women, there is some mysterious effect, so their fame is extraordinarily great, which is a case of the drunkard's intention not being in the wine.

Supplement to the Local News of Shenbao

Talking

Stratosphere Exploration 233

— Su

Recently, newspapers have been publishing news about the Belgian scientist Piccard's stratosphere exploration. It is said that he ascended to 16,000 meters in a hot air balloon and stayed in the air for 15 hours, and the results were very satisfactory. What exactly is the stratosphere? How should it be explored? Readers may not be very clear, so here is a simple explanation:

As we know, the Earth is surrounded by air. Common experience tells us that the higher the altitude, the lower the air temperature. However, after reaching a certain altitude, the temperature no longer decreases even if we ascend further. It is as if the air is divided into two layers, the lower layer is called the troposphere, where the air temperature decreases rapidly with altitude. The upper layer is called the stratosphere, where the air temperature does not vary with altitude. The height of the stratosphere varies depending on the location. At 50 degrees north latitude, it is about seven miles; at the equator, it is about ten miles; and at the North and South Poles, it is only about five miles.

Recently, scientists from various countries have been paying close attention to the exploration of the stratosphere, and they have been trying various methods to explore the special phenomena of the stratosphere. The tools they commonly use rely on hot air balloons. There are two types of balloons, large and small. The large ones are called sounding balloons, and they are equipped with sophisticated meteorological instruments. After ascending to high altitude, people inside can measure the air pressure, temperature, and humidity of the stratosphere. The small ones are called pilot balloons, with a diameter of only about twenty inches. They have a simpler structure and are released by meteorological stations in various countries every day.

The maximum altitude reached by manned balloons (sounding balloons) is about ten miles. The maximum altitude reached by pilot balloons is more than twelve miles. The altitude reached by airplanes is far less, only about seven or eight miles.

What is the thickness of the stratosphere? This question cannot be answered definitively at present. However, according to general speculation, the temperature in the space from at least six miles to more than twenty-two miles above can definitely be constant.

Most of the various chaotic phenomena in the air are caused by uneven temperatures. Because the temperature is the same everywhere in the stratosphere, the air in the stratosphere does not have phenomena such as heating, cooling, expansion, and contraction like the air in the troposphere. Therefore, all phenomena such as clouds, storms, dryness, and humidity can only exist in the troposphere.

Although the reason why the stratosphere exists is still unknown, it has a very significant impact on meteorology. Therefore, scientists from various countries have been conducting stratosphere exploration one after another. It is expected that in the near future, there will be unexpected discoveries.

Regarding "The Headliner" and So On 234

— Yang Cunren

A piece by Mr. [Shaobo], titled [Reconciliation], was published in the [Torch] section of the [Great Evening News]. It used every trick in the book to sow discord between me and Mr. Lu Xun, and it also took the opportunity to slander and accuse me personally. It seems to have been written in a state of [righteous indignation]. [Spitting blood on people] is still a bit hot, which is quite shocking! (Naturally, only I am shocked; this should be stated). Moreover, it critically attacked my [Return from the Red Zone] in a fragmented and exaggerated manner. It seems that his [righteous indignation] is worthy of admiration and worship by the [young masses]. However, I believe that the reality may be beyond his expectations.

First, I would like to ask, my [Return from the Red Zone] was a series of articles published in the [Social Daily]. What does it have to do with me that the editor put it at the end? At the same time, Mr. Lu Xun's article was placed at the beginning by the editor because it was a special manuscript for the public. What does this have to do with Mr. Lu Xun and me? [The headliner] is a specialty of Beijing opera troupes. My [Return from the Red Zone] is not a novel and does not deserve this honor, and I do not dare to take on the role of the [headliner] actor. I must first respectfully decline. And tell Mr. [Shaobo] that this time [the art of scolding people] is not applied skillfully.

Second, my [Return from the Red Zone] reported the situation of the Red Bandits in an objective manner, especially the feelings at that time in the paragraph describing the desolate streets of Pingfang after the disaster. It was said entirely in a realistic style. Why is this not allowed? Should I distort reality to deceive readers? Mr. [Shaobo] attacked my description and believed that the current Red Zone is a place [going to the masses], and it should be described as a paradise. This does not make clear what his ideology is. Is it that [going to the masses] only means the current Red Zone? That is one thing; secondly, [young people followed the leaders of the intellectual world and made many miserable efforts, and some even sacrificed their precious lives for this]. Is it believed that the current Red Zone is a paradise, so they made efforts and sacrifices? I declare first that my ideological concepts at the time when I went to the Red Zone were not like that. At the same time, I also believe that many young people were not like that. Mr. [Shaobo] is certainly [filled with righteous indignation], but no one sympathizes with you. Moreover, I believe that young people will immediately scold you for conducting counter-propaganda. I also believe that there will be people following you to scold me, but I believe that your ability to incite is still very weak.

Having been unreasonably scolded and slandered for raising the banner of petty-bourgeois revolutionary literature and advocating the theory of revolutionary romanticism is already [commonplace]. Unexpectedly, now I am suffering for others because of the editing methods of the magazine editor. This is unavoidable to make people laugh bitterly. I would like to take this opportunity to hope that the gentlemen of the petty-bourgeois intelligentsia can give me an impartial and fair critique with theory? If anyone gives me an impartial and fair theoretical critique, I will accept it. However, the reason for hoping that the petty-bourgeois intelligentsia will speak is that Mr. Lu Xun told me not to mention [the proletarian masses], and the reason for hoping that there is a theory to criticize me is that I have only seen the left-wing theorist Gu Fei unreasonably scold me in his article, and I have heard that Mr. Lu Xun even ridiculed me a few times, and I have appreciated the boring sketches in the cartoons, and I have heard slanders, accusations, and malicious words.

Originally, I knew that you young gentlemen would definitely come out to [speak out for justice], especially Mr. Lu Xun, who would definitely launch a counter-attack, so I did not need to defend myself. However, I also knew that in people's [speaking out for justice] and launching counter-attacks, I would inevitably be ridiculed and ridiculed in an unreasonable manner, so I spoke for myself. (September 1)

The Night of Bombing Taiwan 235

— Xin Qin

For someone who hadn't enjoyed a proper bath for three years, that afternoon, they got to float on the sea entirely; initially feeling extremely delighted, gradually they felt utterly exhausted. Upon climbing ashore and getting dressed, it was already sunset. With a slight headache and mildly aching feet, stepping into the twilight, I went straight to a nearby friend's house. Coincidentally, I was invited as a guest by the host, and amidst unenthusiastic drinking, my listless mood was unintentionally carried away by the gentle, cool breeze. The mat was laid out in the courtyard, and under the misty twilight, waves of fresh, invigorating sensations permeated my heart and soul, making me involuntarily exclaim inwardly:

[What a tranquil place!...]

When the drinking ended and the guests dispersed, the air was already filled with a deep, thick night atmosphere. We felt as if we had entered another human realm, feeling light and relaxed all over. The three of us walked together past the flowers and trees veiled by lamplight, stepped out of the gate, and disappeared into the night road where the cool breeze frequently blew.

The night wind blew through the leaves, rustling, echoing the sound of our shivering footsteps on the grassy field. We all laughed happily, continuing to exclaim:

Home
